                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202405921-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/61d1f586-0b64-41dd-8929-ce622f9fa1f5/smll202405921-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/61d1f586-0b64-41dd-8929-ce622f9fa1f5/smll202405921-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/60cc0769-2044-4562-a046-6489cac6a603/smll202405921-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/61d1f586-0b64-41dd-8929-ce622f9fa1f5/smll202405921-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202405921-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202405921" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrode kinetic analysis of molybdenum-modified hard carbon materials. a) Nyquist plots at the initial state. b) Warburg coefficient fitting curves. c,d) GITT curves and calculated D<sub>app, Na</sub> of the HC and Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 samples, respectively. e) CV curves, f) Fitting diagrams for Peak 1 and Peak 2, g) Capacitive contribution at different scan rates, h) Capacitive and diffusion contribution at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> of Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0. i) Comparison of the structural parameters and electrochemical properties of HC and Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The unmodified HC sample has a larger Warburg coefficient (<i>σ</i>), indicating a slower diffusion capacity. The apparent migration dynamics of sodium ions throughout the entire charge–discharge process are further investigated using galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5c,d</a> and Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16 and S17</a> (Supporting Information). The calculated average apparent Na ion diffusion coefficient (D<sub>app, Na</sub>) for Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 is ≈10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, significantly higher than that of the HC electrode, which is corroborated with EIS fitting results.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0061_R_d38791517e1988" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Chem. Eng. J.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The diffusion coefficients of Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-2.5, Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0, Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-7.5, and Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-10 electrodes exhibit similar evolutionary trends, further confirming the similar hard carbon structure with Mo modification and rich pseudo-graphite carbons. Both EIS and GITT tests reveal that molybdenum modification enhances electrode kinetics and ionic transport dynamics.</p>
            
            <p>To further investigate the energy storage mechanism of the electrode material, dynamic analysis is conducted based on CV curves. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5e</a> shows the CV measurement curves from 0.1 to 5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. The measured peak current (<i>i</i>) and scan rate (<i>v</i>) exhibit a power-law relationship of <i>i = av<sup>b</sup></i>, where <i>a</i> is an adjustable constant and <i>b</i> is the slope value of linear fitting of log<i>i</i> and log<i>v</i>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0062_R_d38791517e2027" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Energy Environ. Sci.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Typically, the <i>b</i> value near 0.5 implies that the electrochemical behavior of electrode is primarily influenced by diffusion, while the <i>b</i> value near 1 suggests that the process is controlled by capacitance. The fitted b values for peaks 1 and 2 of Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5f</a>) are 0.43 and 0.51, respectively, which suggests that Na<sup>+</sup> storage process is mainly diffusion-controlled. It is owing to the predominant presence of pseudo-graphite carbon in Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0, where sodium ions are primarily stored through insertion and extraction, resulting in the predominant role of diffusion. Furthermore, the contributions of diffusion and capacitance to the specific capacity at different scan rates for Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 are calculated (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5g</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0063_R_d38791517e2052" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Carbon">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5h</a> presents the diffusive and capacitive contribution chart at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. In this case, the diffusion contribution dominates, accounting for 93%. It can be noticed that the contribution of capacitance gradually increases to 66% as the scan rate increases (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a>, Supporting Information). It implies that the sodium storage mechanism is largely capacitively controlled at high scan rates, resulting in faster electrochemical kinetics and excellent rate capability for Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0. A comparison of the structural parameters and electrochemical properties of two samples is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5i</a> (with that of HC designated as 1), which reveals the excellent performance of Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0.</p>
            
            <p>The structural evolution of the Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 electrode during charging and discharging is further investigated by utilizing in situ Raman spectroscopy, as illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0006">6</a>. As the potential varied from 1.2 to 0.1&nbsp;V in the discharge phase, the D band progressively widens, suggesting that the sodium ions in the sloping region were primarily governed by adsorption.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0013_R_d38791517e2083" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Conversely, in the plateau region, while the D peak remains constant, the position of the G peak shifts reversibly (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0006">6a,b</a>). This shift is linked to charge transfer resulting from the intercalation of sodium ions, which causes an elongation of the C─C bond, thereby inducing a redshift of the G band. With the shift of the G peak, the I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub> values fluctuate regularly, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information). With further discharge, the G peak undergoes a significant red shift to 1574 cm<sup>−1</sup>. Concurrently, a new peak emerges at 1463 cm<sup>−1</sup> within the G band. The newly formed peaks from G-band splitting are related to the boundary layer of Na-GIC.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0030_R_d38791517e2104" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Energy Lett.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This may be attributed to the fact that the molybdenum-modified hard carbon with sufficient pseudo-graphite domains provides active sites for the insertion of sodium ions, thus enhancing the plateau capacity of the anode material. Moreover, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0005">5</a>, the sodium ion storage process is mainly controlled by diffusion, further suggesting that sodium ions are stored by inserting pseudo-graphitic carbon. Notably, the G peak has not fully returned to its initial value yet, which suggests that the small amount of sodium ions inserted into Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 cannot be completely removed. Furthermore, it also demonstrates that this activation is not a singular occurrence, but can persist in subsequent processes<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0012_R_d38791517e2114" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Energy Mater.">12</a>, <a href="#smll202405921-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0064_R_d38791517e2114" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Adv. Energy Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In situ Raman spectra with time-potential of the Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 electrode during the second discharge/charge process (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0006">6c,d</a>) corroborate with the view above. In the plateau region below 0.1&nbsp;V, sodium ions are inserted into pseudo-graphitic carbons forming the new peak. Meanwhile, the G peak is reversibly shifted by charge transfer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202405921-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0065_R_d38791517e2125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Adv. Energy Mater.">65</a>-<a href="#smll202405921-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202405921-bib-0067_R_d38791517e2125" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Based on the in situ Raman test and other tests mentioned above, the structural comparison schematic of HC to Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 is drawn in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202405921-fig-0006">6e</a>. Through the modification of molybdenum and high-temperature carbonization treatment, the increase in pseudo-graphitic carbons content in Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 provides sites for the insertion of large numbers of sodium ions. By reducing the specific surface area while suppressing the occurrence of side reactions, anode materials with high capacity, high ICE, and stable cycling stability were obtained.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202405921-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/01aae235-f7b6-4d49-b22e-f6414422b1c3/smll202405921-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/01aae235-f7b6-4d49-b22e-f6414422b1c3/smll202405921-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bbb3379a-6dd8-4b8a-8787-8805d68d0bf1/smll202405921-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/01aae235-f7b6-4d49-b22e-f6414422b1c3/smll202405921-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202405921-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202405921" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">In situ Raman characterization. a,b) In situ Raman spectroscopy of Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 during the first discharge/charge process. c,d) In situ Raman spectra with time-potential of the Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 electrode during the second discharge/charge process. e) Schematic diagram of the structural comparison from HC to Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202405921-sec-0050">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202405921-sec-0050-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In this work, we report a high-pseudo-graphite carbon hard carbon strategy by constructing Mo-modified hard carbon solid spheres, which comprehensively improve the sodium storage capacity, cycling stability, ICE, and rate performance of HC. The Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 anode possesses a substantial amount of pseudo-graphitic carbons (69.53%), serving as sites for insertion/extraction of sodium ions to enhance the plateau capacity. With fewer defects and a small specific surface area of 6.94 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>, Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 reduces the interaction between the electrode and electrolyte and irreversible reactions, which contributes to improved ICE and cycling stability. Additionally, the introduced C─Mo interface bond enhances interface stability and reaction kinetics, resulting in outstanding cycling properties. Consequently, the prepared Mo<sub>2</sub>C/HC-5.0 demonstrates comprehensive enhanced performance with a high specific capacity of 410.7&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, a high ICE of 83.9%, excellent cyclic performance (214.9&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 800 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, with a capacity retention rate of 94.8%), and rate performance (140.3&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>). The approach seems to hold great potential for driving the progress of SIBs for applications in large-scale energy storage.</p>
         </section>

                  <li data-bib-id="smll202405921-bib-0003"><span class="bullet">3</span><span class="author">X. X. He</span>, <span class="author">W. H. Lai</span>, <span class="author">Y. Liang</span>, <span class="author">J. H. Zhao</span>, <span class="author">Z. Yang</span>, <span class="author">J. Peng</span>, <span class="author">X. H. Liu</span>, <span class="author">Y. X.
